<review>Recently moved to the area and needed a new groomer for my dog. Although there are a good amount of 1 star ratings I thought I would give them a try since their overall was a 4.0 rating and to be honest there are not a lot of small business groomers in the area. The people were very friendly and the groomer asked and listened to what kind of cut I wanted. When I picked up my dog she had one of the worst haircuts I've ever seen her get (and there was only one other time I felt this way about a cut my dog got). I‚Äôm not picky at all and usually don‚Äôt mind a little bit of choppiness cause it just grows back..Her body looked uneven which was pretty bad, but I could see past, but her face was SO CHOPPY. I had to use my husband's clippers to try my best to fix it. It was that bad that I felt the need to fix it immediately when we got home. Her cut was nothing like her head shape too! She looked like a different dog. They cut it short down the center of her face then longer around the sides like she had a middle part. Her ears weren't even trimmed..I'm not sure if I got someone new. I love supporting small grooming businesses and the people were very friendly, but for the price (which was a bit higher where I usually go to) I don't plan to ever go back. I really contemplated calling to bring my dog back to have them try to fix it, but decided I didn't want to risk her coming back worse. I want to add that my dog gets tons of cuts (every 3 months) so I know she is good when she gets groomed so I'm not sure how she messed up so badly :/ she is a Pomeranian poodle mix, but her hair is like a Pomeranian. Lastly, I dropped my dog off at 12 noon and they told me she would be done at 4pm which is long for a cut. Places like petco take 4 hours and I know they leave dogs in crates, which is why I only go to smaller grooming businesses that usually only take 2-2.5hours so I was already hesitant. After 4 hours I don‚Äôt receive any call that she's done and the store was closing in an hour. I finally call and the woman on the phone immediately says ‚Äúoh, she's done‚Äù..I don't know how long my dog was just waiting there because I never received a call and I don't know how much longer she would've been waiting if I never reached out and called myself... also, usually the groomer will hand you your dog at the end and personally thank you, but she didn't. Someone else brought my dog out..I usually never write reviews unless a place is outstanding because great businesses deserve great reviews or unless my experience is horrible enough for me to want to warn future customers. A one star rating is brutal, but it is a reflection of the experience I had :/ seems like others can say the same ...</review>< Pics>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
Acton Market is the main market for the town of Acton.  It is a new version of the old store that was located across the street.  Acton Market has an excellent grocery selection as well as a delicious/meat market and pastry shop and cafe kiosk.  The pastries and some breads are baked at the store every day and the prices are very good.  There is a small, chance, parking lot and the employees are all small-town friendly.  I sometimes stop in just to buy a coffee drink, some fresh guacamole (seasonal), or a fruit tart!

This is a great place to visit.  It is located in the quiet town of Acton which is filled with ranch-style homes, quaint old churches, vintage western-style buildings, and an occasional movie star.</text>

< text>
Beware of ordering subcontracted work from Home Depot! They don‚Äôt have your back.

We purchased a Dekton countertop from Home Depot in 2016, based on a long list of features that convinced us that this was the highest quality product. The sales brochure lists ‚Äúimpact resistance‚Äù among its many assets: notably this feature no longer appears in their sales material.

Home Depot contracts Plamar to perform the fabrication of the countertops. From the moment of delivery and installation we noticed irregularities and outright flaws along the majority of the exposed edges, especially around the radiused corners of the sink cutout. Within a couple of weeks we had a nickel sized chip become knocked out of one of these corners, caused by a thin wine glass that got knocked over. Plamar sent a worker with some plain glue to ‚Äúrepair‚Äù it, but we turned it down as no more than patchwork. This is the full extent that Plamar has ever supported us.

Dekton is distributed and represented by Cosentino in the Bay Area. At the time they were responsive and sent a factory technician (from Spain) to examine and repair the problem. He indicated that the Plamar fabrication was substandard and that training was essential. We were satisfied with their engagement, until the corner chip that had been repaired came apart again, without any duress.

Since then we have engaged Home Depot, Plamar and Cosentino to have them address the recurring fault. Each has passed the buck to the other in a never-ending hot potato of non-responsibility.

Home Depot has been totally disengaged and ineffective in being a customer advocate to resolve the ongoing problems with the product they sold us. The department head, Nancy, and store manager, Jose Marquez, have not returned our calls or emails, nor have they offered any assistance. I cannot recommend Home Depot for countertops, denounce their contractor Plamar as a shoddy and irresponsible fabricator, and Cosentino an unreliable material supplier who does not stand behind their marketing claims or warranty.< /text>

Just adding an update to the review I wrote below. It is almost a month past when they said my order would arrive. I paid thousands in advance. I sat on hold to speak with a Pro-desk representative at the Soquel California store. I waited for approximately 15 minutes and then someone picked up the phone and hung it up before saying "hello". <Pics>None< /Pics>< Text>
Home Depot has a ton of stuff, and generally at very good prices. It's my go-to for almost any hardware. They have a good return policy as well. My only concern is that the level of knowledge of the staff is hit-and-miss ... sometimes they are knowledgeable, and sometimes they aren't. This can result in (a) getting good advice, (b) getting redirected to somebody who knows a lot, or (c) getting bad advice. I've frequently found the floor staff to be a bit surly when I ask where to find something. All that said, I still go to Home Depot first unless I have a specialized request.</Text>

<UserId.>106713914240470940178< /UserId.><username>Robert Castillo</username><time>1498623092278<//time><rating>3<//rating>< review>
I give this store a solid "Meh" rating. It's ok. Like any box store they value quantity over selection. They don't always have what you need, but if they do, they have lots of it! The items they have are reasonably priced and they typically have at least a single choice within most quality ranges. Where some stores might have the quality categories of Good/Better/Best this store has ok/good/pretty good.

As for the employee knowledge and courtesy, well, it's a bit spotty. Some of the employees I've asked for help are very knowledgeable, helpful, and patient. Others are too busy talking with other employees or have no idea where to find anything in their own workplace. I once asked an employee where to find fuel line for a lawnmower and got the response "I'm not sure. Maybe you should ask somebody". He wasn't being rude, just clueless.

I will say that the people there to help with self checkout are always quick to help and so far I've had hassle free returns, but the lady who advertises the children's activities is way too pushy and gets irritating quickly. And the solar people who hassle you every time you walk in there treat you like a second class citizen when they find out you live in a mobile home. It's like they're irritated with you for wasting their time after they hassled you.

With this store I feel like there is a good side for every bad and enough of both to warrant my continued patronage with limited expectations.</review>
